Past"], "abstract": "<jats:p>Abstract. Late Pleistocene sea level has been reconstructed from ocean sediment core data using a wide variety of proxies and models. However, the accuracy of individual reconstructions is limited by measurement error, local variations in salinity and temperature, and assumptions particular to each technique. Here we present a sea level stack (average) which increases the signal-to-noise ratio of individual reconstructions. Specifically, we perform principal component analysis (PCA) on seven records from 0 to 430\u202fka and five records from 0 to 798\u202fka. The first principal component, which we use as the stack, describes \u2009\u223c\u2009\u202f80\u202f% of the variance in the data and is similar using either five or seven records. After scaling the stack based on Holocene and Last Glacial Maximum (LGM) sea level estimates, the stack agrees to within 5\u202fm with isostatically adjusted coral sea level estimates for Marine Isotope Stages\u00a05e and 11 (125 and 400\u202fka, respectively). Bootstrapping and random sampling yield mean uncertainty estimates of 9\u201312\u202fm (1\u03c3) for the scaled stack. Sea level change accounts for about 45\u202f% of the total orbital-band variance in benthic \u03b418O, compared to a 65\u202f% contribution during the LGM-to-Holocene transition. Past"], "abstract": "<jats:p>Abstract. We present a compilation of 127 time series \u03b413C records from\nCibicides wuellerstorfi spanning the last deglaciation\n(20\u20136\u2009ka) which is\nwell-suited for reconstructing large-scale carbon cycle changes, especially\nfor comparison with isotope-enabled carbon cycle models. The age models for\nthe \u03b413C records are derived from regional planktic\nradiocarbon compilations (Stern and Lisiecki,\u00a02014). The\n\u03b413C records were stacked in nine different regions and then\ncombined using volume-weighted averages to create intermediate, deep, and\nglobal \u03b413C stacks. These benthic \u03b413C stacks\nare used to reconstruct changes in the size of the terrestrial biosphere and\ndeep ocean carbon storage. The timing of change in global mean\n\u03b413C is interpreted to indicate terrestrial biosphere\nexpansion from 19\u20136\u2009ka. The \u03b413C gradient between the\nintermediate and deep ocean, which we interpret as a proxy for deep ocean\ncarbon storage, matches the pattern of atmospheric CO2 change\nobserved in ice core records. The presence of signals associated with the\nterrestrial biosphere and atmospheric CO2 indicates that the compiled\n\u03b413C records have sufficient spatial coverage and time\nresolution to accurately reconstruct large-scale carbon cycle changes during\nthe glacial termination.\n                    </jats:p>", "DOI": "10.5194/cp-14-1229-2018", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2018, 8, 16]], "date-time": "2018-08-16T06:07:59Z", "timestamp": 1534399679000}, "page": "1229-1252", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 1, "title": ["Deglacial carbon cycle changes observed in a compilation of 127 benthic \u03b413C time series (20\u20136&thinsp;ka)"], "prefix": "10.5194", "volume": "14", "author": [{"ORCID": "http://orcid.org/0000-0003-1839-7299", "authenticated-orcid": false, "given": "Carlye D.", "family": "Peterson", "sequence": "first", "affiliation": []}, {"given": "Lorraine E.", "family": "Lisiecki", "sequence": "additional", "affiliation": []}], "member": "3145", "published-online": {"date-parts": [[2018, 8, 16]]}, "reference": [{"key": "ref1", "unstructured": "Allen, K.\u00a0A., Sikes, E.\u00a0L., H\u00f6nisch, B., Elmore, A.\u00a0C., Guilderson,\nT.\u00a0P.,\nRosenthal, Y., and Anderson, R.\u00a0F.: Southwest Pacific deep water carbonate\nchemistry linked to high southern latitude climate and atmospheric\nCO2\nduring the last glacial termination, Quaternary Sci. 117 time series &amp;amp;#948;&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;13&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;C records from Cibicides wuellerstorfi spanning the last deglaciation (20&amp;amp;#8211;6&amp;amp;#8201;kyr) and well-suited for reconstructing large-scale carbon cycle changes, especially for comparison with isotope-enabled carbon cycle models. The age models for the &amp;amp;#948;&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;13&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;C records are derived from regional planktic radiocarbon compilations (Stern and Lisiecki, 2014). The &amp;amp;#948;&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;13&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;C records were stacked in nine different regions and then combined using volume-weighted averages to create intermediate, deep, and global &amp;amp;#948;&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;13&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;C stacks. These benthic &amp;amp;#948;&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;13&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;C stacks are used to reconstruct mean changes in the size of the terrestrial biosphere and deep ocean carbon storage. The timing of change in global mean &amp;amp;#948;&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;13&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;C is interpreted to indicate terrestrial biosphere expansion from 19&amp;amp;#8211;6&amp;amp;#8201;ka. The &amp;amp;#948;&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;13&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;C gradient between the intermediate and deep ocean, which we interpret as a proxy for deep ocean carbon storage, matches the pattern of atmospheric CO&amp;lt;sub&amp;gt;2&amp;lt;/sub&amp;gt; change observed in ice core records. The presence of signals associated with the terrestrial biosphere and atmospheric CO&amp;lt;sub&amp;gt;2&amp;lt;/sub&amp;gt; indicates that the compiled &amp;amp;#948;&amp;lt;sup&amp;gt;13&amp;lt;/sup&amp;gt;C records have sufficient spatial coverage and time resolution to accurately reconstruct large-scale carbon cycle changes during the glacial Past"], "abstract": "<jats:p>Abstract. The fact that the deep-ocean benthic \u03b413C minimum shifted from the North Pacific to the South Atlantic during the Last Glacial Maximum is often interpretted as evidence of a change in deep water circulation, such as the development of deep water ventilation in the North Pacific or a decrease in Southern Ocean overturning. This study re-evaluates the implications of changes in benthic \u03b413C gradients by comparing Pacific Deep Water (PDW) \u03b413C measurements with the values expected for the null hypothesis that PDW ventilation sources remained unchanged throughout the Late Pleistocene. The \u03b413C compositions of PDW, Northern Component Water (NCW) and Southern Component Water (SCW) are estimated from regional benthic \u03b413C stacks of 3\u20136 sites. Changes in PDW \u03b413C and PDW-SCW \u03b413C gradients over the past 800 kyr are found to be well described by a constant mixture of 60% NCW and 40% SCW plus a constant Pacific remineralization offset of \u22120.5\u2030. Thus, a change in PDW ventilation cannot be inferred solely on the basis of changes in the Pacific-South Atlantic benthic \u03b413C gradient.\n                    </jats:p>", "DOI": "10.5194/cp-6-305-2010", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2010, 5, 7]], "date-time": "2010-05-07T06:09:41Z", "timestamp": 1273212581000}, "page": "305-314", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 12, "title": ["A simple mixing explanation for late Pleistocene changes in the Pacific-South  Atlantic benthic \u03b413C gradient"], "prefix": "10.5194", "volume": "6", "author": [{"given": "L. Past Discuss."], "abstract": "<jats:p>Abstract. The fact that the deep-ocean benthic \u03b413C minimum shifted from the North Pacific to the South Atlantic during the Last Glacial Maximum is often interpretted as evidence of a change in deep water circulation, such as the development of deep water ventilation in the North Pacific. This study re-evaluates the implications of changes in benthic \u03b413C gradients by comparing Pacific Deep Water (PDW) \u03b413C measurements with the values expected for the null hypothesis that PDW ventilation sources remained unchanged throughout the Late Pleistocene. The \u03b413C compositions of PDW, Northern Component Water (NCW) and Southern Component Water (SCW) are estimated from regional benthic \u03b413C stacks of 3\u20136 sites. Changes in PDW \u03b413C and PDW-SCW \u03b413C gradients over the past 800 kyr are found to be well described by a constant mixture of 60% NCW and 40% SCW plus a constant Pacific \"age\" offset of \u22120.5\u2030. Thus, an additional ventilation source for glacial PDW (e.g., in the North Pacific) cannot be inferred solely on the basis of changes in the Pacific-South Atlantic benthic \u03b413C gradient.\n                    </jats:p>", "DOI": "10.5194/cpd-5-2607-2009", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2010, 4, 29]], "date-time": "2010-04-29T13:13:26Z", "timestamp": 1272546806000}, "page": "2607-2630", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 1, "title": ["A simple mixing explanation for late Pleistocene changes in the Pacific-South Atlantic  benthic &delta;13C gradient"], "prefix": "10.5194", "volume": "5", "author": [{"given": "L. Past Discuss."], "abstract": "<jats:p>Abstract. Late Pleistocene sea level has been reconstructed from ocean sediment core data using a wide variety of proxies and models. However, the accuracy of individual reconstructions is limited by measurement error, local variations in salinity and temperature, and assumptions particular to each technique. Here we present a sea level stack (average) which increases the signal-to-noise ratio of individual reconstructions. Specifically, we perform principal component analysis (PCA) on seven records from 0\u2013430 ka and five records from 0\u2013798 ka. The first principal component, which we use as the stack, describes ~80 % of the variance in the data and is similar using either five or seven records. After scaling the stack based on Holocene and Last Glacial Maximum (LGM) sea level estimates, the stack agrees to within 5 m with isostatically adjusted coral sea level estimates for Marine Isotope Stages 5e and 11 (125 and 400 ka, respectively). When we compare the sea level stack with the \u03b418O of benthic foraminifera, we find that sea level change accounts for about ~40 % of the total orbital-band variance in benthic \u03b418O, compared to a 65 % contribution during the LGM-to-Holocene transition. Additionally, the second and third principal components of our analyses reflect differences between proxy records associated with spatial variations in the \u03b418O of seawater.\n                    </jats:p>", "DOI": "10.5194/cpd-11-3699-2015", "type": "journal-article", "created": {"date-parts": [[2015, 8, 13]], "date-time": "2015-08-13T09:23:25Z", "timestamp": 1439457805000}, "page": "3699-3728", "source": "Crossref", "is-referenced-by-count": 10, "title": ["A Late Pleistocene sea level stack"], "prefix": "10.5194", "volume": "11", "author": [{"given": "R.
